Both arrays should have the same length N.  If\\n10570:         only `x` is given (and ``y=None``), then it must be a two-dimensional\\n10571:         array where one dimension has length 2.  The two sets of measurements\\n10572:         are then found by splitting the array along the length-2 dimension. In\\n10573:         the case where ``y=None`` and `x` is a 2xN array, ``linregress(x)`` is\\n10574:         equivalent to ``linregress(x[0], x[1])``.\\n10575: \\n10576:         .. deprecated:: 1.14.0\\n10577:             Inference of the two sets of measurements from a single argument `x`\\n10578:             is deprecated will result in an error in SciPy 1.16.0; the sets\\n10579:             must be specified separately as `x` and `y`.\\n10580:     alternative : {'two-sided', 'less', 'greater'}, optional\\n10581:         Defines the alternative hypothesis. The square of ``rvalue``\\n10601:             is equal to the coefficient of determination.\\n10602:         pvalue : float\\n10603:             The p-value for a hypothesis test whose null hypothesis is\\n10604:             that the slope is zero, using Wald Test with t-distribution of\\n10605:             the test statistic. See `alternative` above for alternative\\n10606:             hypotheses.\\n10607:         stderr : float\\n10608:             Standard error of the estimated slope (gradient), under the\\n10609:             assumption of residual normality.\\n10610:         intercept_stderr : float\\n10611:             Standard error of the estimated intercept, under the assumption\\n10612:             of residual normality.\\n10613: \\n10614:     See Also\\n10615:     --------\\n10616:     scipy.optimize.curve_fit :\\n10617:         Use non-linear least squares to fit a function to data.\\n10618:     scipy.optimize.leastsq :\\n10619:         Minimize the sum of squares of a set of equations.\\n10620: \\n10621:     Notes\\n10622:     -----\\n10623:     For compatibility with older versions of SciPy, the return value acts\\n10624:     like a ``namedtuple`` of length 5, with fields ``slope``, ``intercept``,\\n10625:     ``rvalue``, ``pvalue`` and ``stderr``, so one can continue to write::\\n10626: \\n10627:         slope, intercept, r, p, se = linregress(x, y)\\n10628: \\n10629:     With that style, however, the standard error of the intercept is not\\n10630:     available. Default is 'two-sided'.\\n10582:         The following options are available:\\n10583: \\n10584:         * 'two-sided': the slope of the regression line is nonzero\\n10585:         * 'less': the slope of the regression line is less than zero\\n10586:         * 'greater':  the slope of the regression line is greater than zero\\n10587: \\n10588:         .. versionadded:: 1.7.0\\n10589: \\n10590:     Returns\\n10591:     -------\\n10592:     result : ``LinregressResult`` instance\\n10593:         The return value is an object with the following attributes:\\n10594: \\n10595:         slope : float\\n10596:             Slope of the regression line.\\n10597:         intercept : float\\n10598:             Intercept of the regression line.\\n10599:         rvalue : float\\n10600:             The Pearson correlation coefficient.
